  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8f0115bc-16ce-485a-8e11-ee20a139ab79'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17508240510455983624">Praised for its epic scope and descriptive detail, <i>Across the Nightingale Floor</i>, the first book in the Tales of the Otori series, was an international bestseller and critical success, named by the <i>London Times</i> as "the most compelling novel to have been published this year." With <i>Grass for His Pillow</i>, Book Two, we return to the medieval Japan of Lian Hearn's creation—a land</span>
  <span id="freeText17508240510455983624" style="display:none">Praised for its epic scope and descriptive detail, <i>Across the Nightingale Floor</i>, the first book in the Tales of the Otori series, was an international bestseller and critical success, named by the <i>London Times</i> as "the most compelling novel to have been published this year." With <i>Grass for His Pillow</i>, Book Two, we return to the medieval Japan of Lian Hearn's creation—a land of harsh beauty and deceptive appearances.In a complex social hierarchy, amid dissembling clans and fractured allegiances, there is no place for passionate young love. The orphan Takeo has been condemned to work as an assassin—an enforced occupation that his father sacrificed his own life to escape. Meanwhile, Takeo’s beloved Shirakawa Kaede, heir to the Murayama and alone in the world, must find a way to unify the domain she has inherited, as she fights off the advances of would-be suitors and hopes against fading hope that Takeo will return to her...</span>
  <a data-text-id="17508240510455983624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9096761897441365325">After the emotional events of the first book, the two lovers in this Japanese Shogunate-ish fantasy are split up. He's on the road and she must defend her new position as the head of her household. Winter is coming, indeed, in this tragic -- and beautiful -- setting.<br/><br/>Tone and setting are where this book shines, but the main characters have really grown into their own even if their situations are rather horrible. Or you know their situations are only going to get REALLY bad soon, anyway. :)<br/><br/>These A</span>
  <span id="freeText9096761897441365325" style="display:none">After the emotional events of the first book, the two lovers in this Japanese Shogunate-ish fantasy are split up. He's on the road and she must defend her new position as the head of her household. Winter is coming, indeed, in this tragic -- and beautiful -- setting.<br /><br />Tone and setting are where this book shines, but the main characters have really grown into their own even if their situations are rather horrible. Or you know their situations are only going to get REALLY bad soon, anyway. :)<br /><br />These ARE tragedies. Tearjerker tragedies. <br /><br />And damn... I hate to say this, but all these old-time Japanese are just THUGS. Murderous brigands pretending to be honorable. Just... wow.</span>

<div id="review_2649399383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2649399383" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2649399383?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780733615634" href="/book/show/9334575-grass-for-his-pillow">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2649399383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5263805928960783793"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547213137ra/26901774.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The emotional turmoil doesn't let up. And to think I already know what will happen so I should be prepared!<br/><br/>This second book starts shortly after the first. Takeo has been taken hostage by the Tribe and is kept in a secret house so Arai's forces can't find him (Arai, thinking Takeo betrayed him, is furious). Kaede, meanwhile, convinces Arai to let her go to her family's estate for now, only to find it in shambles and severely damaged. Not only natural catastrophes (earthquakes, typhoons and the l</span>
  <span id="freeText5263805928960783793" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547213137ra/26901774.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The emotional turmoil doesn't let up. And to think I already know what will happen so I should be prepared!<br><br>This second book starts shortly after the first. Takeo has been taken hostage by the Tribe and is kept in a secret house so Arai's forces can't find him (Arai, thinking Takeo betrayed him, is furious). Kaede, meanwhile, convinces Arai to let her go to her family's estate for now, only to find it in shambles and severely damaged. Not only natural catastrophes (earthquakes, typhoons and the likes) but also mismanagement and her father losing a battle against Arai's forces are to blame. Her father, shunning daughters no matter how intelligent they are and blaming them for making him too weak to kill himself honourably, finally agrees to teach Kaede how to manage estates.<br>There is also Kaede's neighbour, a nobleman from the capital called Fujiwara, who consideres her a rare jewel to be collected.<br><br>It doesn't really matter which group of people we look at - Kaede's father with his retainers, Fujiwara and his, the Tribe - they are all the most despicable human beings imaginable. From how Kaede's father talks about his daughters <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and the fact that he actually started desiring her in a sexual way and then tries to not only force her to commit suicide but to rape her before that <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the Tribe ordering Yuki to sleep with Takeo in order to get a child with his abilities - as if she was a breeding mare - and her and Kenji not objecting <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I didn't know who I wanted to die first.<br><br>Once again, it's a tactful, beautifully written tale that very accurately describes a fictional (but very realistic) feudal Japan. Nevertheless, the author managed to subtly include female characters that at least see the problem with the system and are trying to break free.<br><br>One of the most heartbreaking things in this second installment was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Kaede lost Takeo's child <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. However, my heart also broke when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Takeo actually slept with Yuki - and repeatedly <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Sure, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there hadn't been any promises technically. But he felt guilty, proving that he knows he's doing something wrong, something that will hurt Kaede when she finds out. And he constantly thinks about her and his inner monologues proclaim his undying love for her so how could he nevertheless sleep with another woman?! And don't give me "biological reasons" because at this point in the tale he still had two intact hands <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>!<br><br>Most of all, though, I hate the hypocrisy and lies of these people. They talk about honour but what, for example, is honorable about 13-year-olds and even younger children having to kill themselves when their disgraced fathers take their own lives?! It’s just an easy way for the victors of a conflict of getting rid of entire rival bloodlines. As usual, however, these bullies are really good at hiding any rottenness in fine silks. Disgusting!<br>Another great example for the pretense of honour and community is the Tribe itself, of course. It came as no surprise to me when we discovered who had killed Takeo's biological father. But it is frustrating beyond belief how these people, time and time again, are getting away with such behaviour.<br>The ending of this installment was therefore balm for my soul, which is why I hated that prophecy so much!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5263805928960783793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2295595373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7439441534560455646">This read was me giving this series a second shot. After not enjoying the first book, I decided to carry as it has really good ratings here on goodreads. Unfortunately, as much as it pains me to abandon a series, especially one by an Aussie author, I will not be continuing on.<br/><br/>I had the exact same issues with this book as I did with the first. Mainly, it was just boring. For a book about politics, warriors and war it is just so damn predictable. The writing was beautiful (as in the first) but thi</span>
  <span id="freeText7439441534560455646" style="display:none">This read was me giving this series a second shot. After not enjoying the first book, I decided to carry as it has really good ratings here on goodreads. Unfortunately, as much as it pains me to abandon a series, especially one by an Aussie author, I will not be continuing on.<br /><br />I had the exact same issues with this book as I did with the first. Mainly, it was just boring. For a book about politics, warriors and war it is just so damn predictable. The writing was beautiful (as in the first) but this did not save it for me.<br /><br />My other issue was this book was the excessive occurrence of characters threatening to or committing seppuku. Nearly every single character at some point, says they are going to commit suicide because they have 'dishonoured' themselves. It was so frequent it lost all impact and quite frankly became a bit offensive.</span>

  <i>“Death comes suddenly and life is fragile and brief. No one can alter this either by prayers or spells.”</i>
</blockquote><br/></span>

<div id="review_2753444609" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2753444609" />
    <a title="Edward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13459162-edward"><img alt="Edward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579803798p2/13459162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2753444609?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/13459162-edward">Edward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13459162-edward?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13459162-edward?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2753444609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10715591196160207630">Grass for His Pillow is the second book of the Tales of the Otori series by Lian Hearn.<br/><br/>Now before I begin, I must say that I really enjoyed the first book. Sure, it had cliches and elements about it that I would usually not enjoy, but I found it an excellent read. I love the fantasy Japanese inspired world as it is one of my passions and the world-building is very strong.<br/><br/><b>‘I did not want to kill him. But I did.’</b><br/><br/>However, Grass for His Pillow was a lot slower. After reading over 300 pages I am left</span>
  <span id="freeText10715591196160207630" style="display:none">Grass for His Pillow is the second book of the Tales of the Otori series by Lian Hearn.<br /><br />Now before I begin, I must say that I really enjoyed the first book. Sure, it had cliches and elements about it that I would usually not enjoy, but I found it an excellent read. I love the fantasy Japanese inspired world as it is one of my passions and the world-building is very strong.<br /><br /><b>‘I did not want to kill him. But I did.’</b><br /><br />However, Grass for His Pillow was a lot slower. After reading over 300 pages I am left with the feeling that nothing really happened. Seeing the development of characters within the first book was one of the reasons why I loved The Nightingale Floor so much, but book 2 contains near to no development in my opinion.<br /><br />Unfortunately, it felt like a very shallow read. A filler and preparation book for what is to become for Takeo and Kaede. But, I did finish it! Lian Hearn has great prose and her writing, descriptions and structure is all very good.<br /><br /><b>'She shared the same deep sorrow but no tears came to her eyes. She would allow nothing to weaken the power that was coming to life within her.’</b><br /><br />I will carry on the series, because Takeo is a great character and the books ended on a sort of cliffhanger, but it won’t be my priority within my tbr pile for now.<br /><br />(It might not help that I’ve been reading dad’s first draft of A TIME OF COURAGE alongside this. I’m not biased but it’s very hard for a book to hold up against that. Wow…)<br /><br /><b>‘In the Tribe I was known as the Dog, but I preferred to think of myself like this wolf, no longer owned by anyone.’</b><br /><br />2.5/5 - A book that flows well but all in all leaves you feeling like not that much has happened with the characters. But I’m sure it will ramp up in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10715591196160207630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_236522107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236522107" />
    <a title="Petros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6984857-petros"><img alt="Petros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321523871p2/6984857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236522107?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petros" href="/user/show/6984857-petros">Petros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer236522107&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236522107" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9530299239141928061">The second book is about the aftermath of the fall of the evil Tohan by a new warlord named Arai; all of which happen out of screen, since showing takes effort compared to just throwing in an infodump. The new warlord ain’t any better than the Tohan, since he also kills anyone who disagrees and plans to waste the protagonist and anyone around him just to make sure he won’t turn against him next. Something which the hero eventually does because he would be killed if he didn’t, therefore the new v</span>
  <span id="freeText9530299239141928061" style="display:none">The second book is about the aftermath of the fall of the evil Tohan by a new warlord named Arai; all of which happen out of screen, since showing takes effort compared to just throwing in an infodump. The new warlord ain’t any better than the Tohan, since he also kills anyone who disagrees and plans to waste the protagonist and anyone around him just to make sure he won’t turn against him next. Something which the hero eventually does because he would be killed if he didn’t, therefore the new villain is an idiot. <br /><br />Kaede, the hero’s sweetheart, is pregnant after that morbid sex scene in the previous book, and lies about the identity of the father in an attempt to save both of their lives. So yeah, Shigeru, the good feudal lord from the first book, is now the father, and Arai is stupid enough to believe he can’t kill his baby without causing a rebellion from all those who loved Shigeru. A rebellion that never happened when Shigeru was killed, but will somehow happen by the death of an unborn baby. <br /><br />Kaede returns to her palace, in a territory ruined by wars, bad harvests, and a semi-crazy man who happens to be her father. Once again the world building is the best part of the book, since we get to fully understand what it’s like to live in a feudal society where honor is above all, to the point hara-kiri is the ultimate expression of it. It’s all about following traditions, being obedient, and gutting yourself when something goes terribly wrong. <br /><br />It’s the character motivations that come off ham-fisted because of author Lian’s dislike of male sexism, as she constantly makes the lords ridiculing Kaede every time she wants to take the initiative and help out her father in restoring the land. There is a difference between telling a woman to shut up because she has a vagina and acting like a complete jerk; but author Lian doesn’t bother to tell which is which. She even goes as far as having Kaede’s crazy father trying to rape her like the asshole male he is, before getting killed by the deus ex machina of a ninja, which the hero trained with in the first book. <br /><br />After that lazy resolution, the ninja helps her out in gaining control of the household by killing everyone who doesn’t accept her as his leader. Something which is evil when a man like Arai does it, but very heroic when Kaede does it… with the help of a man. Feminism for the win, right guys? Yes, it’s supposed to represent how there is no good or evil in the society they are living in, since everyone needs to dirty his hands in order to get on top of things. The way it was portrayed though doesn’t feel like that, since Kaede is clearly favored over any other man. What follows the violent take over, is her falling ill and miscarriages, thus being victimized in the eyes of the reader. See guys? Arai didn’t lose his baby. Kaede did, so feel sorry for her even if she is doing the exact same crap as the villain. <br /><br />In the meantime, our hero Takeo is trained harshly by the ninjas in order to become a ruthless killer. He learns all sorts of ninja tricks and even kills some poor guys who were marked for death because they did the unforgivable crime of speaking their minds and being liberal. This part is showing again how inhumane this society of obedience really is. It treats people as objects or cattle. Both Kaede and Takeo are seen by their superiors as nothing more than breeders of powerful successors. The ninja masters go as far as having Takeo being seduced by a kunoichi, so she can get pregnant and offer them a ninja offspring with hidden powers such as his. <br /><br />Takeo eventually betrays these assholes after he finds out they also murdered his father for not wanting to kill innocents anymore, and because they use him as nothing more than a stallion for knocking off all their females. Great story for a hentai, but this is not that type of a story. He seeks refuge in the wilderness, where he is aided by the Hidden, the tribe he grew up with. Once more we see Lian doing a lazy job by portraying these people as the obvious victims the reader is supposed to care about, while she is also pretending to keep things grey for both heroes and villains. If you ask me, the only reason these guys are mistreated is because they are pacifists who are never fighting back and author Lian is pro-pacifism. <br /><br />And if you think that wasn’t bad enough, they have their own seer who gives the protagonist a prophecy. OH SHIT HERE WE GO AGAIN! Like a true shounen adventure that has to include a special hero with special powers, fate is working in his favor all the way. He’s not simply a super ninja, he also has noble blood, so he’s allowed to be the ruler of the land. Which he does because the prophesy said so. Great job at ruining the suspense Lian, can I stop reading now since you spoiled the ending? Also, the same prophesy says he will be killed by his own son, so I guess all he has to do is not have any sons. Oh, and thanks for also telling us he didn’t chose to leave the ninjas with his free will; it was God who forced him to do it. Fatalism: taking away the responsibilities of your actions since the invention of religions. <br /><br />After this revelation, plot convenience spiral out of control and Naruto~er, I mean Takeo, keeps getting saved or finds out what he has to do next, with minimal effort. The most improbable random encounters with allies take place, so Takeo can save his life, find Kaede and marry her. And now things are free to can get worse from here. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9530299239141928061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29986-emily?shelf=alternate-history-or-universe">alternate-history-or-universe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29986-emily?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29986-emily?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29986-emily?shelf=badass-complex-women">badass-complex-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29986-emily?shelf=fiction-historical">fiction-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29986-emily?shelf=2011">2011</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164311161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8957749373374041924">I'm calling these books young adult as well as for adults, though I think the only reason I think of them as young adult is because the protagonists are in their late teens. These are definitely books I would have read and loved as a teenager; there's no explicit sex though lots of reference to it, and the violence is hardly as graphic as you see in movies.<br/><br/>Anyway, genre descriptions aside, this is a brilliant trilogy and I am literally only pausing long enough to write my review of book two befo</span>
  <span id="freeText8957749373374041924" style="display:none">I'm calling these books young adult as well as for adults, though I think the only reason I think of them as young adult is because the protagonists are in their late teens. These are definitely books I would have read and loved as a teenager; there's no explicit sex though lots of reference to it, and the violence is hardly as graphic as you see in movies.<br /><br />Anyway, genre descriptions aside, this is a brilliant trilogy and I am literally only pausing long enough to write my review of book two before getting back in bed to start book three. I love both the heroes here; Takeo's journey to find out where his true obligations (and his heart) lie is inspiring and sympathetic all at once, and Kaede is turning into quite the feminist pioneer. I really appreciate how the author has not fallen into the trap that some fantasy writers do, by putting an entirely modern feminist mindset into the mind of someone brought up in the medieval world; Kaede struggles with being a "proper" woman by society's standards and worrying all the time what people will think, yet she goes on doing what she must in order to protect herself and her sisters, and it only makes me love her more. I am loving this series so much, I am on absolute tenterhooks to find out how it's going to resolve. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8957749373374041924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText16946620610214726309" style="display:none">I liked this book well enough, though it suffered a bit from middle-book syndrome. <div id="review_42013182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42013182" />
    <a title="Jeph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1869845-jeph"><img alt="Jeph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1236757686p2/1869845.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42013182?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeph" href="/user/show/1869845-jeph">Jeph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42013182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3597773356753938401">Lian Hearn's "Grass for his Pillow" is a must-continue for fans of "Across the Nightingale Floor", and resumes the story of Otori Takeo and Shirakawa Kaede, of the first book, but leaves much to be desired in terms of plot, action and everything else that made Hearn's first entry in this series so magical and endearing.<br/><br/>"Grass" picks up almost exactly where "Across" left off. Takeo is now with the Tribe and much of the book focuses on Kaede trying to claim her inheritance of domain, meanwhile fen</span>
  <span id="freeText3597773356753938401" style="display:none">Lian Hearn's "Grass for his Pillow" is a must-continue for fans of "Across the Nightingale Floor", and resumes the story of Otori Takeo and Shirakawa Kaede, of the first book, but leaves much to be desired in terms of plot, action and everything else that made Hearn's first entry in this series so magical and endearing.<br /><br />"Grass" picks up almost exactly where "Across" left off. Takeo is now with the Tribe and much of the book focuses on Kaede trying to claim her inheritance of domain, meanwhile fending off suitors who wish to marry her while she holds out hope for marrying Takeo. Everything that readers found in the first book is still here in the second book, but dull and toned down. At many times the book involves itself in unimportant matters and spends too much time in certain areas. Perhaps this was to build plot points or grant insight into the characters and the world they inhabit, but the pages spent seem to cross the line into dragging the book along at an almost unbearable pace.<br /><br />Perhaps this was a stylistic choice of pacing and setting, as much of the book takes place over a period of harsh winter. By the time spring arrives, both the characters and readers are anxious for action, movement and the new possibilities that lie ahead now that the snows have melted.<br /><br />If you enjoyed "Across the Nightingale Floor", by all means read "Grass for his Pillow" if only just to continue following the story that surrounds the characters, but don't expect the book to suck you in. You will only be left with a feeling of waiting for something more... the next book perhaps...</span>
  <a data-text-id="3597773356753938401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137311050?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karissa" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa">Karissa</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137311050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15060031220756616894">This is the second book in the Tales of the Otori series by Lian Hearn. This book picks up where the first left off. Takeo leaves Kaede for training under the mysterious Tribe; whose supernatural abilities Takeo has inherited from his father. As his training concludes, and he is asked to take out certain missions, he must ask himself if his loyalties will lie with the Tribe or with the Otori? Kaede meanwhile is left on her own to return home and see what state her family is in. Kaede struggles t</span>
  <span id="freeText15060031220756616894" style="display:none">This is the second book in the Tales of the Otori series by Lian Hearn. This book picks up where the first left off. Takeo leaves Kaede for training under the mysterious Tribe; whose supernatural abilities Takeo has inherited from his father. As his training concludes, and he is asked to take out certain missions, he must ask himself if his loyalties will lie with the Tribe or with the Otori? Kaede meanwhile is left on her own to return home and see what state her family is in. Kaede struggles to consolidate her power and claim the inheritance she was left in a world that is run by men.<br /><br />This was a fitting second book for this series. It moved along at the steady, descriptive pace of the second book. Although for some reason I found myself getting bored while reading this book. The lush descriptions, while detailed, didn't bring the book to life in the way I hoped they would. I had a little trouble understanding some of the stupid decisions made by Kaede and Takeo along the way. Despite these misgivings, if you liked the first book you must read the second book. It is very much in the same style of the first book and continues the story of Kaede and Takeo. This book definitely builds to a climax preparing you for the war and conflict of the third novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15060031220756616894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_101716618" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101716618" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101716618?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781573222518" href="/book/show/1147722.Grass_for_his_Pillow">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101716618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4792815482475296520">This being the second, in a planned trilogy, I felt it was more of a "place holder" or a "where we are now" kind of book. It reminds me of The Empire Strikes Back. It's a continuation of the story of the characters we've come to love, but not much happens. We get a lot more back story, but not a whole lot of action, other than to put our heroes in a harder spot. That's okay, I already have the third book on my nightstand waiting to be read.:)<br/><br/>The Japan that Hearn has created is beautiful. I gener</span>
  <span id="freeText4792815482475296520" style="display:none">This being the second, in a planned trilogy, I felt it was more of a "place holder" or a "where we are now" kind of book. It reminds me of The Empire Strikes Back. It's a continuation of the story of the characters we've come to love, but not much happens. We get a lot more back story, but not a whole lot of action, other than to put our heroes in a harder spot. That's okay, I already have the third book on my nightstand waiting to be read.:)<br /><br />The Japan that Hearn has created is beautiful. I generally seek out Asian settings anyway, but she has taken the truth of Japan and made it even more mystical, fantastic, gorgeous and rich. I have no trouble believing the embellishments she has added to the culture. The special skills she gives the Tribe just seem to me to be a natural extension of the abilities this warrior country has realistically honed for millenium. That some should be born with abilities beyond most of us is completely reasonable to me. I find it even more interesting that she does not limit these skills and gifts to men. There are women gifted in the Tribe as well. <br /><br />I'm anxious to read the next installment, and am actually glad that her planned trilogy has now become five books. I have a feeling Hearns Middle Heaven will be hard to leave.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4792815482475296520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1429199-becca?shelf=must-own-someday">must-own-someday</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198231724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1219631258550613045">For a middle-book in a trilogy, this one was really fabulously done, with the exception that it should have been longer. I love where the story-line is going even though I'm not sure where it will end up, the characters (which I thought were fabulous for the most part in the first book) have really grown on me, and the relationships that have developed are full and interesting. <br/><br/>One thing I really like about this author so far is she isn't afraid to subject her characters to the greatest pain pos</span>
  <span id="freeText1219631258550613045" style="display:none">For a middle-book in a trilogy, this one was really fabulously done, with the exception that it should have been longer. I love where the story-line is going even though I'm not sure where it will end up, the characters (which I thought were fabulous for the most part in the first book) have really grown on me, and the relationships that have developed are full and interesting. <br /><br />One thing I really like about this author so far is she isn't afraid to subject her characters to the greatest pain possible or even kill them when the story and its players deem death necessary. And she does it in a emotionally rending way. I could hardly tear myself away from the pages until I knew what happened.<br /><br />Kaede has absolutely stolen my imagination. I am rooting so hard for her! Can't wait to see what happens next and her growth. I hope her power she has found doesn't diminish because of her rash choices at the end of this book. *crossing fingers*</span>

<div id="review_1404848121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1404848121" />
    <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley"><img alt="Pam Baddeley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442488147p2/42764850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1404848121?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam Baddeley" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley">Pam Baddeley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330415262" href="/book/show/1182983.Grass_for_His_Pillow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=teen-or-young-adult">teen-or-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1404848121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6662353559661387542">This second volume in the Otori trilogy commences at the point where book 1 left off. Faced with an ultimatum from the Tribe, his biological father's people, to either join them and finish his training with them, renouncing his inheritance from his adoptive father Otori Shigeru, or else be killed, Takeo has to go with them. (Takeo's adoption into the Otori clan is later declared illegal by the self serving uncles who arranged for Shigeru's murder in any case). He then endures privations and puni</span>
  <span id="freeText6662353559661387542" style="display:none">This second volume in the Otori trilogy commences at the point where book 1 left off. Faced with an ultimatum from the Tribe, his biological father's people, to either join them and finish his training with them, renouncing his inheritance from his adoptive father Otori Shigeru, or else be killed, Takeo has to go with them. (Takeo's adoption into the Otori clan is later declared illegal by the self serving uncles who arranged for Shigeru's murder in any case). He then endures privations and punishments to make him comply, but it is clear that some of those among the Tribe resent his gifts and his possible supplanting of themselves in his Tribe family's hierarchy so are working their own agendas.<br /><br />Left behind, Shirakawa Kaede has major problems of her own, finding her mother has died and her father has more or less suffered a breakdown after being unable to stop warriors travelling through his land enroute to the fighting which now has broken out between lord Arai and the former supporters of the dead warlord Iida Sadamu. Her father still has loyalties to the opponents of Lord Arai although Arai now expects Kaede to ally herself to him. The house and grounds are in poor order, as are the lands around, thanks to a combination of natural disasters and the ongoing fighting. A local lord then develops a fascination with Kaede: he is known to prefer men, but wants to 'collect' her and add her to his collection, something which would entail her having to marry him - which she is under pressure to do - and then being more or less sequestered for the rest of her life. Despite this she manages to convince her father to start teaching her - giving her a son's education as she only knows the script used by women - so that she can understand the estate accounts and know everything she needs in order to take over management of the estate which he has neglected for a long time. She also tries to protect her sisters. <br /><br />The obstacles in the way of Kaede and Takeo ever marrying seem insurmountable, and political events are escalating. Only with allies can Kaede take the inheritance of the richer lands that her dead kinswoman intended she should have and can she and Takeo gain the resources they need as a power base.<br /><br />In a lot of ways this is a typical middle book in a trilogy. It takes the characters forward in their personal timelines and development but not a great deal happens plotwise. Some of the things set up at the start of the book do not pan out as expected <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ for instance, Kaede miscarries the child she conceived when she and Takeo made love on the night of Iida's death, thinking they would not survive <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There are ominious indications of future threats as well as the immediate ones. The fantasy version of medieval Japan is again beautifully evoked with the very different attitudes, compared to Western ones, to honour, suicide and religion.<br /><br />For me, the ending was a bit rushed and didn't quite gell with what has been developed up to now - the two main characters act out of a more Western style viewpoint than the one their culture would dictate. So I can only give this a 4 star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6662353559661387542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ilana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59371159-ilana"><img alt="Ilana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563253235p2/59371159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3196920793?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/24955288-grass-for-his-pillow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=medieval">medieval</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=japan">japan</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3196920793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14483787298491566577">From April 2011 — (3.5 stars) At the end of <i>Across the Nightingale Floor,</i> Takeo was kidnapped by members of the Tribe, a clan of murderers who are intent on making him one of theirs. Having inherited an uncommon number of exceptional gifts from his father, he is of great value to them. Here we find Takeo at first fighting them off and attempting to flee, without success. They eventually wear him down and he gives his word that he will stay with the Tribe, even as his heart yearns for Kaede. But </span>
  <span id="freeText14483787298491566577" style="display:none">From April 2011 — (3.5 stars) At the end of <i>Across the Nightingale Floor,</i> Takeo was kidnapped by members of the Tribe, a clan of murderers who are intent on making him one of theirs. Having inherited an uncommon number of exceptional gifts from his father, he is of great value to them. Here we find Takeo at first fighting them off and attempting to flee, without success. They eventually wear him down and he gives his word that he will stay with the Tribe, even as his heart yearns for Kaede. But Takeo is soon wrapped up in the harsh and difficult training that is required of him and even takes on a lover. Meanwhile, Kaede makes her way back to her family's estate to find that it has fallen in a state of disrepair and poverty. Her father, who has fallen prey to mental illness since Kaede's mother's death, is unable to fulfill his duties and after many attempts and cajoling, she eventually convinces him to teach her skills which are only known to men so that she can take over the running of the estate and secure an army to realize great plans ahead.<br /><br />Takeo and Kaede's individual struggles were interesting to observe, as is the evolution of both characters from inexperienced youths to committed and driven adults. But I can't say I quite as taken with this book as I was with the first one. That being said, the groundwork is set up for what promises to be a thrilling ride in the third book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14483787298491566577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2322799245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_431696183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/431696183" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1564654-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222373756p2/1564654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/431696183?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/1564654-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1564654-mark?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer431696183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2384890488606738519">I enjoyed reading <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77160.Across_the_Nightingale_Floor__Tales_of_the_Otori___1_' title='Across the Nightingale Floor (Tales of the Otori, #1) by Lian Hearn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Across the Nightingale Floor</a>
</i> quite a bit, but my mistake was that I didn't buy the sequels at the same time. By the time I remembered to get them, two years had passed and, possibly because of that time away from Takeo's world, I didn't enjoy this second volume nearly as much. For the first several chapters I was completely lost as to who was whom (despite reading Wikipedia's largely useless recap of <i>Across the Nightingale Floor</i> beforehand), and by the time I started rememb</span>
  <span id="freeText2384890488606738519" style="display:none">I enjoyed reading <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77160.Across_the_Nightingale_Floor__Tales_of_the_Otori___1_" title="Across the Nightingale Floor (Tales of the Otori, #1) by Lian Hearn" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Nightingale Floor</a>
</i> quite a bit, but my mistake was that I didn't buy the sequels at the same time. By the time I remembered to get them, two years had passed and, possibly because of that time away from Takeo's world, I didn't enjoy this second volume nearly as much. For the first several chapters I was completely lost as to who was whom (despite reading Wikipedia's largely useless recap of <i>Across the Nightingale Floor</i> beforehand), and by the time I started remembering the characters' interrelationships I was halfway through the book. The additional problem, I think, is that this book suffers from "act two syndrome," in which the excitement of the first book gives way to the setup to the climax--and the setup is never as fun as the climax itself. This book read like filler to me; the author was positioning her characters for the final volume of the trilogy. Nothing wrong with that (it has to be done, of course), but I'd been hoping for something in addition to that setup. I think I can safely take the blame for most of my dislike of this book (the two-year reading gap between this one and the first one) but I'm nonetheless confident that this one isn't as good as the first one. But I'm looking forward to the third one anyway--and this time I'm not waiting two years to read it....</span>
  <a data-text-id="2384890488606738519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117250839?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lenny" href="/user/show/4141624-lenny">Lenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781573222518" href="/book/show/1147722.Grass_for_his_Pillow">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117250839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13099094749534959531">Like others have mentioned, 'Grass For His Pillow' is a bridge, obviously leading up to events in the third book. While the book is slow, the language is still flowery and engaging, and I am continually intrigued by the complicated web of politics and honor. I greatly appreciate how the Tribe's abilities are supernatural, yet it does not feel like fantasy or magic.<br/><br/>However, I am finding it exceedingly difficult to establish an emotional, immediate connection with the main characters, Takeo and Ka</span>
  <span id="freeText13099094749534959531" style="display:none">Like others have mentioned, 'Grass For His Pillow' is a bridge, obviously leading up to events in the third book. While the book is slow, the language is still flowery and engaging, and I am continually intrigued by the complicated web of politics and honor. I greatly appreciate how the Tribe's abilities are supernatural, yet it does not feel like fantasy or magic.<br /><br />However, I am finding it exceedingly difficult to establish an emotional, immediate connection with the main characters, Takeo and Kaede. Takeo speaks in first person, but as if he is retelling the story many years later. Kaede is spoken in the third person, and many of her thoughts come through guarded dialogue, and not her own thoughts. Their emotions weren't raw, immediate and messy; instead they felt distant and artificial. It is frustrating that the more engaging characters, like Shigeru and Maruyama, are either peripheral characters or dead.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to the next book, and hopefully it will be more fast-paced and emotional.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13099094749534959531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/6960931-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6960931-andrew?shelf=japan">japan</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240913453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5368218296323259258">Compelling enough, but felt to me more like an interlude between the start and conclusion of the trilogy. It has been many years since I read the first book, so it took a considerable amount of time for me to remember the events that took place in it. But even still, I felt like the emotional pitch of the book was a bit flat. There were a few exciting moments, but even the situations that should have been powerful lacked the impact they should have had. It's possible that was intentional to evok</span>
  <span id="freeText5368218296323259258" style="display:none">Compelling enough, but felt to me more like an interlude between the start and conclusion of the trilogy. It has been many years since I read the first book, so it took a considerable amount of time for me to remember the events that took place in it. But even still, I felt like the emotional pitch of the book was a bit flat. There were a few exciting moments, but even the situations that should have been powerful lacked the impact they should have had. It's possible that was intentional to evoke the emotionally muted nature of Japanese society at the time, but it doesn't make for the best storytelling. If there is one thing Hearn does very well though, it is evoking a complete picture of the world the story takes place in. In some ways, I found the settings and environments of the stories more compelling than the characters. <i>Grass for his Pillow</i> may not be completely successful, but there is still enough to like here to make me want to read the conclusion of the trilogy.</span>

<div id="review_527913161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527913161" />
    <a title="littlemiao" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/544621-littlemiao"><img alt="littlemiao" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200260028p2/544621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527913161?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="littlemiao" class="user" itemprop="url" name="littlemiao" href="/user/show/544621-littlemiao">littlemiao</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527913161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9038450094180823729">2017 - I am still enjoying this series more than I did the first time I read it. I never got to the final book so I am re-reading everything to prepare myself. Maybe the second reading allows me to appreciate some of the more poetic qualities of the narrative, and not get caught up in whatever elements (predictability, characterization?) irritated me the first time. It is a well-constructed story, and well-told.<br/><br/>---------<br/>2013 - I have to admit that the ending came as a shock, not because I was su</span>
  <span id="freeText9038450094180823729" style="display:none">2017 - I am still enjoying this series more than I did the first time I read it. I never got to the final book so I am re-reading everything to prepare myself. Maybe the second reading allows me to appreciate some of the more poetic qualities of the narrative, and not get caught up in whatever elements (predictability, characterization?) irritated me the first time. It is a well-constructed story, and well-told.<br /><br />---------<br />2013 - I have to admit that the ending came as a shock, not because I was surprised by the concluding event, but because not enough had happened in the story to justify a conclusion. Nothing particularly climactic, since in my mind, the last event (no spoilers) was fairly predictable. It seemed like it was cut off just for the sake of getting another book out of it. Still, it is obviously setting the stage for something dramatic and I am invested enough to keep going.<br /><br />The fact that the male protagonist is in first person and the female protagonist is in third person seems a little odd to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9038450094180823729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282023279?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/1812322-sandy">Sandy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sandy by: </span>
      Chamness
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=poc">poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=fantasy-classic">fantasy-classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=alternating-viewpoints">alternating-viewpoints</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=strong-girls">strong-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1812322-sandy?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282023279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10450433498882866478">In this book, our hero Takeo figures out over the course of about 200 pages that all of the decisions he made at the climatic end of the first volume (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77160.Across_the_Nightingale_Floor__Tales_of_the_Otori___1_' title='Across the Nightingale Floor (Tales of the Otori, #1) by Lian Hearn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Across the Nightingale Floor</a>) were stupid. He then spends the last 100 pages attempting to undo these decisions and set things right - the act of which promises to cause the conflict that will drive the last book in the trilogy since aparently the timing is no longer right so now the "right" decisions are actually bad decisions. <br/><br/>Honestly, Kaede's </span>
  <span id="freeText10450433498882866478" style="display:none">In this book, our hero Takeo figures out over the course of about 200 pages that all of the decisions he made at the climatic end of the first volume (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77160.Across_the_Nightingale_Floor__Tales_of_the_Otori___1_" title="Across the Nightingale Floor (Tales of the Otori, #1) by Lian Hearn" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Nightingale Floor</a>) were stupid. He then spends the last 100 pages attempting to undo these decisions and set things right - the act of which promises to cause the conflict that will drive the last book in the trilogy since aparently the timing is no longer right so now the "right" decisions are actually bad decisions. <br /><br />Honestly, Kaede's character saves the story for me. She's developed nicely as a character and I enjoyed watching her take charge of her own life. Yay strong women.<br /><br />Snarkiness aside, this really wasn't a terrible book. I do admit that character stupidity aside the writing is engaging, and I'm curious to see how the series wraps up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10450433498882866478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer166001715247632993">I think the series has grown on me, I am finding the writing in the 2nd book to be much better quality, and my complaint with the last book about detail has been rectified in this book. The pacing is slower than in the first book, though I have found this slowing down to be well compensated by the rise in quality of the prose.<br/>Upto now I don't agree with the general opinion that this book is somehow lesser than the first one, on the contrary it may be better.<br/>After finishing this book one can see </span>
  <span id="freeText166001715247632993" style="display:none">I think the series has grown on me, I am finding the writing in the 2nd book to be much better quality, and my complaint with the last book about detail has been rectified in this book. The pacing is slower than in the first book, though I have found this slowing down to be well compensated by the rise in quality of the prose.<br />Upto now I don't agree with the general opinion that this book is somehow lesser than the first one, on the contrary it may be better.<br />After finishing this book one can see that the first book serves to pull in the readers with its fast pace and interesting characters and setting and the second book as is the case with most intermediate books serves to build upon and consolidate the world building and characterization from the first novel,<br />I will be diving into the third novel directly.</span>

<div id="review_316405870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/316405870" />
    <a title="Ambrosia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1811588-ambrosia"><img alt="Ambrosia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386472866p2/1811588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/316405870?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ambrosia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ambrosia" href="/user/show/1811588-ambrosia">Ambrosia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1811588-ambrosia?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer316405870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16494143972696511533">While the plot structure of this second book in the series is a little less traditional than the first, that actually works in many ways to its advantage. Both of the main characters are trying to find their identity in various ways, and while the plot is far less action-oriented, I found the character development associated with their internal struggles to make them far more compelling than they were in the first book. Towards the end, when Takeo sees Kaede and observes how much they've both ch</span>
  <span id="freeText16494143972696511533" style="display:none">While the plot structure of this second book in the series is a little less traditional than the first, that actually works in many ways to its advantage. Both of the main characters are trying to find their identity in various ways, and while the plot is far less action-oriented, I found the character development associated with their internal struggles to make them far more compelling than they were in the first book. Towards the end, when Takeo sees Kaede and observes how much they've both changed, I was pleased to discover that I agreed and could readily trace their development.<br /><br />The narrative still has some weaknesses, largely due to the aforementioned lack of action and some stylistic issues. But the lovely poetic language is still firmly in place, and there are definite storm clouds on the horizon. I'm looking forward to the third book.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16494143972696511533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YgT0YBtSd+VxXdgCaqxRqILbZpvGljaBFa37wSKEJNDkmmzx3kXLVvvFjnygBa7GyRpMnRspA21dtbOg8K9Jfg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qYceGIR+OfRaepqrRzSi1HQhO0wn2oMPT1ndcEl0dIAvGYaJQWmFR9DizNWNnV26P+ARSvpltuMHQZURm18ZLg==')})
  }

All rights reserved.The sound was stabbing, slicing, shivering, like metal scraping against stone. Eragon\'s teeth vibrated in sympathy, and he covered his ears with his hands, grimacing as he twisted around, trying to locate the source of the noise. Saphira tossed her head, and even through the din, he heard her whine in distress.Eragon swept his gaze over the courtyard twice before he noticed a faint puff of dust rising up the wall of the keep from a foot-wide crack that had appeared beneath the blackened, partially destroyed window where Blödhgarm had killed the magician. As the squeal increased in intensity, Eragon risked lifting a hand off one ear to point at the crack.&quot;Look!&quot; he shouted to Arya, who nodded in acknowledgment. He replaced his hand over his ear.Without warning or preamble, the sound stopped.Eragon waited for a moment, then slowly lowered his hands, for once wishing that his hearing was not quite so sensitive.Just as he did, the crack jerked open wider--spreading until it was several feet across--and raced down the wall of the keep. Like a bolt of lightning, the crack struck and shattered the keystone above the door to the building, showering the floor below with pebble-sized rocks. The whole castle groaned, and from the damaged window to the broken keystone, the front of the keep began to lean outward.&quot;Run!&quot; Eragon shouted at the Varden, though the men were already scattering to either side of the courtyard, desperate to get out from under the precarious wall. Eragon took a single step forward, every muscle in his body tense as he searched for a glimpse of Roran somewhere in the throng of warriors.At last Eragon spotted him, trapped behind the last group of Derfor er det også på tide, at Danmark får sin helt egen E L James. Hun hedder Pernille Vørs, og med Spillet om sirenen indleder hun sin Dominic-trilogi, der fortæller historien om det lidenskabelige, men farlige forhold mellem den dæmoniske Ian Dominic og den eventyrlystne Catharina Julie Hansen.\n\nCatharina Julie Hansen er et smukt rodehoved af en rødtop på 24 år, som netop har fået nyt arbejde på en jetset-restaurant. Her møder hun Ian Dominic, en lidt ældre, mystisk mangemillionær, der tillige er en yderst eftertragtet ungkarl. \n\nCatharina indlader sig i stadig højere grad med denne manipulerende, dæmoniske drømmemand. Først som en art selskabsdame, senere som Ians mellemleder på restauranten og ikke mindst som hans elskerinde. De to hvirvles ind i et accelererende, eksperimenterende seksuelt spil, der hurtigt kommer til at fylde deres liv. Trods deres modsætninger kommer de tættere på hinanden og nærmer sig noget, der til forveksling kunne minde om ægte kærlighed. Dog bærer de begge rundt på en familietragedie, der truer med at knuse deres forhold. Kan lidenskaben overleve, eller må de erkende, at deres forhold er dødsdømt? \n\nSpillet om sirenen er første bind i Dominic-trilogien. \n\nUddrag af bogen: \n\n”Jeg er ikke i stand til at elske.” Ordene bliver sagt lavt og en anelse forsigtigt, men jeg hører vigtigheden i hans toneleje. ”Jeg har heller aldrig haft trangen til det, så det er ikke noget, som jeg har savnet.”\n\nMine øjne begynder at svide, for jeg er ikke dum. Ian er i gang med at fortælle mig, at han godt ved, at jeg har følelser for ham, og at han ikke er i stand til at gengælde dem, samt at han heller ikke har lyst til at gengælde dem.\n\nJeg prøver virkelig på ikke at tage det personligt, men mit hjerte gør så ondt, at det føles, som om min krop bryder sammen. Det var slet, slet ikke det her, som jeg havde tænkt mig. Jeg havde planlagt at få ham til at blive forelsket i tanken om at være forelsket, ikke gøre ham mere sikker i sin sag om, at han aldrig vil forelske sig. Er jeg virkelig så forfærdelig at være forelsket i?\n\nJeg er overrasket over, hvor stærk min stemme lyder, ”Har du aldrig været bare en lille smule forelsket?”\n\nHan ser stadig på mig med det blik, der får min krop til at længes efter ham. ”Aldrig, jeg ved ikke, hvordan man gør, jeg tror, at jeg mangler det gen, der skal bruges til det.” Han mener det sgu.\n\nBlikket bliver mere indtrængende og stemmen en smule fastere, ”jeg kan ikke elske, Catharina.” \n\nOm forfatteren:\n\nPernille Vørs (f. 1974) debuterer med Spillet om sirenen.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/43784.Lian_Hearn">About Lian Hearn</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17374609305037772994">Lian Hearn's beloved Tales of the Otori series, set in an imagined feudal Japan, has sold more than four million copies worldwide and has been translated into nearly forty languages. It is comprised of five volumes: ACROSS THE NIGHTINGALE FLOOR, GRASS FOR HIS PILLOW, BRILLIANCE OF THE MOON, THE HARSH CRY OF THE HERON and HEAVEN'S NET IS WIDE. The series was followed by two standalone novels, BLOSS</span>
  <span id="freeText17374609305037772994" style="display:none">Lian Hearn's beloved Tales of the Otori series, set in an imagined feudal Japan, has sold more than four million copies worldwide and has been translated into nearly forty languages. It is comprised of five volumes: ACROSS THE NIGHTINGALE FLOOR, GRASS FOR HIS PILLOW, BRILLIANCE OF THE MOON, THE HARSH CRY OF THE HERON and HEAVEN'S NET IS WIDE. The series was followed by two standalone novels, BLOSSOMS AND SHADOWS and THE STORYTELLER AND HIS THREE DAUGHTERS, also set in Japan. <br /><br />Hearn's forthcoming series: The Tale of Shikanoko will be published by FSG in 4 volumes in 2016. Book 1 will be EMPEROR OF EIGHT ISLANDS out in late-April 2016, followed by book 2: AUTUMN PRINCESS, DRAGON CHILD (June), book 3: LORD OF THE DARKWOOD (August), and the final book (#4) THE TENGU'S GAME OF GO (late-Sept. 2016). <br /><br />Lian has made many trips to Japan and has studied Japanese. She read Modern Languages at Oxford and worked as an editor and film critic in England before immigrating to Australia. </span>

            if ($('bookCover_52797620').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_52797620').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
